Electronics Now tutorial introduces beginners in electronics to basic electronic tools and components needed to start learning about electronics and building circuits.</p>\n\t\t<p>The introduction to electronics is followed by twenty tutorials that use an electronic breadboard to build various circuits. Some of the tutorials use the highly popular Arduino microcontroller board.</p>\n\t\t<div class=\"clr_flt\"></div>\n\t</div>\n\t\n\t<div class=\"area_featured_box\">\n\t\t<h3>Hobby Motor Kit Assembly</h3>\n\t\t<a href=\"/articles/motor-kit-assembly/\"><img src=\"/images/motor-kit.jpg\" alt=\"motor kit\" width=\"375\" height=\"210\"></a>\n\t\t<p>Electric motor kit with multi-ratio reduction gearbox unpacking and assembly. </p>\n\t\t<div class=\"clr_flt\"></div>\n\t</div>\n\t\n\t<div class=\"area_featured_box\">\n\t\t<h3>Arduino Web Server Tutorial – Control an Arduino from a Web Page</h3>\n\t\t<a href=\"/tutorials/arduino/ethernet-shield-web-server-tutorial/\"><img src=\"/images/arduino-web-server.jpg\" alt=\"Arduino and Ethernet Shield\" width=\"375\" height=\"210\"></a>\n\t\t<p>Learn how to turn your Arduino into a web server that allows you to control the Arduino on a web page through the Internet.</p>\n\t\t<p>Turn LEDs on and off, read switch or temperature values from the Arduino in a web browser.</p>\n\t\t<div class=\"clr_flt\"></div>\n\t</div>\n\t\n\t<div class=\"area_featured_box\">\n\t\t<h3>Build a Tiny USB LED Torch</h3>\n\t\t<a href=\"/projects/USB-LED-torch/\"><img src=\"/images/USB-LED-torch.jpg\" alt=\"Home Built USB LED Torch\" width=\"375\" height=\"210\"></a>\n\t\t<p>Build this tiny USB LED torch and power it from a USB power pack or any USB host port.</p>\n\t\t<div class=\"clr_flt\"></div>\n\t</div>\n\t\n\t<div class=\"area_featured_box\">\n\t\t<h3>How to Blow Up a Resistor</h3>\n\t\t<a href=\"/articles/blowing-up-a-resistor/\"><img src=\"/images/blowing-up-resistor.jpg\" alt=\"Burning resistor\" width=\"375\" height=\"210\"></a>\n\t\t<p>This video shows how to blow up a resistor by applying too much power. src=\"/templates/template2/arrow.png\" alt=\"→\"><a href=\"/articles/\"> Articles</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t<img src=\"/templates/template2/arrow.png\" alt=\"→\"><a href=\"/articles/raspberry-PI/\"> Raspberry PI</a>\n\t\t\t\t\t<img src=\"/templates/template2/arrow.png\" alt=\"→\"> Auto Login\t\t</p>\n\t\t<!-- <div id=\"page\"> -->\n\t\t\t<!--<div id=\"r_col\">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t</div>-->\n\n<div id=\"article\">\n\t<h1>Raspberry PI Raspbian Jessie Automatic Login</h1>\n\t<p id=\"page_date\">Created on: 15 June 2016</p>\n\t\t\t<div class=\"google_top_ad\">\n\t\t<script async=\"\" src=\"//pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/js/adsbygoogle.js\"></script>\n\t\t<!-- top_responsive -->\n\t\t<ins class=\"adsbygoogle\" style=\"display: block; height: 250px;\" data-ad-client=\"ca-pub-1311998530216395\" data-ad-slot=\"7918861327\" data-ad-format=\"auto\" data-adsbygoogle-status=\"done\"><ins id=\"aswift_1_expand\" style=\"display:inline-table;border:none;height:250px;margin:0;padding:0;position:relative;visibility:visible;width:275px;background-color:transparent\"><ins id=\"aswift_1_anchor\" style=\"display:block;border:none;height:250px;margin:0;padding:0;position:relative;visibility:visible;width:275px;background-color:transparent\"><iframe width=\"275\" height=\"250\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" vspace=\"0\" hspace=\"0\" allowtransparency=\"true\" scrolling=\"no\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" onload=\"var i=this.id,s=window.google_iframe_oncopy,H=s&amp;&amp;s.handlers,h=H&amp;&amp;H[i],w=this.contentWindow,d;try{d=w.document}catch(e){}if(h&amp;&amp;d&amp;&amp;(!d.body||!d.body.firstChild)){if(h.call){setTimeout(h,0)}else if(h.match){try{h=s.upd(h,i)}catch(e){}w.location.replace(h)}}\" id=\"aswift_1\" name=\"aswift_1\" style=\"left:0;position:absolute;top:0;\"></iframe></ins></ins></ins>\n\t\t<script>\n\t\t(adsbygoogle = window.adsbygoogle || []).push({});\n\t\t</script>\n\t\t<div class=\"clr_flt\"></div>\n\t\t</div>\n\t<p>How to automatically login to the Raspbian operating system on a Raspberry PI. Choose to log in to the command prompt or the graphical desktop without the need to enter a password. Automatically logging in is useful when using the Raspberry PI as a console/kiosk or to run a dedicated application that must auto run at start-up.</p>\n\t<p>In previous versions of Raspbian, the inittab file had to be modified to auto log in. Because of changes to the operating system, Raspbian Jessie no longer has an inittab file in /etc/. With the inittab file gone, the auto login settings can now be changed in the Raspberry PI configuration dialog box as explained in this article.</p>\n\t\n\t<h2>Login Automatically to Raspbian Jessie</h2>\n\t<p>A new installation of Raspbian Jessie automatically logs in and starts the graphical desktop when the Raspberry PI is powered up. Login settings can be changed easily from the desktop.</p>\n\t<p>From the Raspbian desktop, choose <b>Menu → Preferences → Raspberry PI Configuration</b> by using the main menu button at the top left of the screen. The Raspberry PI Configuration dialog box opens with the <b>System</b> tab selected.</p>\n\t<img src=\"raspbian-jessie-menu-button.png\" alt=\"Raspbian Jessie Menu Button\">\n\t<p class=\"pic_caption\">Raspbian Jessie Menu Button</p>\n\t<p>To automatically boot to the command line interface (CLI) at power-up, click the <b>To CLI</b> radio button and make sure that <b>Login as user 'pi'</b> is checked as shown in the image below.</p>\n\t<a href=\"raspbian-jessie-auto-login.png\"><img src=\"raspbian-jessie-auto-login.png\" alt=\"Changing the Raspbian Jessie Auto Login Settings\"></a>\n\t<p class=\"pic_caption\">Changing the Raspbian Jessie Auto Login Settings</p>\n\t\n\t<p>If <b>Login as user 'pi'</b> is checked, you will not have to enter a user name or password when the operating system boots. Selecting <b>To Desktop</b> will boot the Raspberry PI to the graphical desktop. Selecting <b>To CLI</b> will boot the RPI to the command line interface.</p>\n\t<p>The default of the older Raspbian editions was to boot the Raspberry PI to the command line and require a user name and password to log in. This can be set by unchecking \"Login as user 'pi'\" and selecting \"To CLI\".</p>\n\t<p>If you do enable the PI to boot up and require login, don't forget that the default user name is <b>pi</b> and the password is <b>raspberry</b>.</p>\n\t<p>To start the desktop if settings are changed to boot to the command line, enter <b>startx</b> at the command prompt to start the desktop again.</p>\n\t<p>The following video shows how to change from the Raspbian Jessie default of auto login to the desktop to auto login to the command prompt.</p>\n\t<div class=\"clr_flt\"></div>\n<div class=\"you_tube_txt you_tube_txt_width_640\">\n<!--<iframe width=\"\" height=\"\" src=\"//www.youtube-nocookie.com/embed/?rel=0\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe>-->\n\n<iframe class=\"targetblank\" target=\"_blank\">View on YouTube →</a></p>\n</div>\n\t\n\t\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\t\t\t<div class=\"clr_flt\"></div>\n\t\t<div class=\"ad_container\">\n\t\t\t<div
